Jamison Brereton

62 (503)
As╠Бvins
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The first five verses of this hymn cover the familiar ground of A┼Ыvin hymnsтАФthe poetтАЩs eager invitation to the two gods to drive to our sacrifice. Though the theme and sentiments are familiar, there are a number of nice touchesтАФthe enjambment across verse boundaries (1/2a; 2bcd/3a, at least in our opinion) and the play on the concepts of newer and older in verses 4тАУ5. This section ends (5d) with the phrase, modifying the A┼Ыvins, тАЬproviding bright gifts to the singerтАЭ (gr╠ес╣Зate╠Б citra╠Бr─Бt─л).
The following two verses (6тАУ7) touch on several of the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ famous deeds, especially the rescue of Bhujyu from the sea (vs. 6), but the two verses after that (8тАУ9) take a detour, addressing other gods and urging them to take violent action against various enemies. The poet seems so agitated that he loses his grip on gram
mar: verse 9, concerning Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, is syntactically fragmented, shift ing without warning or grammatical agreement between dual and singular and between 3rd and 2nd person. (We have not been able to render the full effect in English.)
Though verse 10 returns us to the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ journey and to a more tranquil gram matical level, it too enlists the A┼Ыvins to attack and also suggests that their journey to us was prompted by the failure of other men. The final verse gives no hint of the agitation in the immediately preceding verses and ends with the same phrase as verse 5, thus implicitly indicating the bipartite structure of the hymn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A┼Ыvins The first part of the hymn is marked by repeated dual prns. opening the vs. or hemistich: 1c y─Б╠Б, 2a, 3a, 4a, 5a t─Б╠Б, 5c y─Б╠Б, 6a t─Б╠Б. This pattern more or less coincides with the division of the hymn discussed in the published introduction. After the beg. of vs. 6 the pattern is broken and does not reappear.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI praise the two leaders of heaven, the presiders over this world; I invoke the A┼Ыvins, glorifying them with sacred hymns, them, who are ever the discomfiture (of foes), who at dawn scatter the investing glooms to the ends of the earth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I shall praise the two outstanding men of this heaven; I call upon the A┼Ыvins, singing [/awakening] with my chantsтАФ
they who, at the breaking of the ruddy dawn, in a single day seek to encompass the ends of the earth and its broad expanses,

Jamison Brereton Notes

Griffith

I LAUD the Heroes Twain, this heaven’s Controllers: singing with songs of praise I call the Asvins,
Fain in a moment, when the morns are breaking, to part the earth’s ends and the spacious regions.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬComing to the sacrifice with their bright splendours, they light up the lustre of (their) car; emitting vast and infinite radiance; they drive their horses over deserts (refreshing them) with water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

While striding to the sacrifice with their gleaming (horses). (The horses) have shone the radiant beam of their chariot through the dusky spaces.
Measuring the many immeasurable expanses, you two drive over the waters, wastelands, and fields,

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. presents both number and person disagreement, the first more acute than the second. As noted above, the vs. begins with the dual NA prn. t─Б╠Б, surely referring to the A┼Ыvins, and this 1st p─Бda ends with an apparent dual part. cakram─Бс╣З─Б╠Б presumably modifying the prn. But the next p─Бda contains a plural verb rurucuс╕е (ruruc┼л in sandhi), which cannot take the dual as subject – nor as object. (Because of its sandhi position cakram─Бс╣З─Б╠Бcould instead reflect underlying pl. -─Б╠Бс╕е, but the initial t─Б╠Бseems almost designed to anchor the participle as dual as well.) Curiously both Geldner and K├╝mmel (431) tr. the dual NP as subj. of the pl. verb without comment – either because of a rare grammatical lapse on their parts or because they view it (without comment) as an example of improper agreement. (It is certainly true that a dual

*rurucatuс╕е would be metrically disastrous, so lax haplology would be thinkable.) I believe that we must take the number and the number disharmony seriously, and I therefore take p─Бdas a and b as separate clauses. The first lacks a finite verb.

We can either consider the participle as predicated (тАЬthey two [are] striding тАжтАЭ) or, my preference, as pendant to 1cd, with dual its subj. As noted in the published introduction, there is another likely enjambment between vss. 2 and 3. The next question is the identity of the pl. subj. of d. There is one pl. form in p─Бda a: instr. pl. ┼Ы├║cibhiс╕е. Geldner and K├╝mmel take this as referring to the r├бjobhiс╕е тАШspacesтАЩ in b, but Renou suggests that it ancitipates the horses (├б┼Ыvaiс╕е) in 3bc. If we accept RenouтАЩs identification of the тАШgleaming onesтАЩ as horses, this provides a possible pl. subj. for rurucuс╕е. As gleaming ones themselves, they could тАЬshine the radiant beam of the chariotтАЭ through the spaces. This may make them sound a little like Rudolph the Red-Nosed Reindeer, but at least it avoids a grammatical solecism.

The ps. disagreement is, by contrast, very mild and standard RVic practice: the dual subj. returns in 2cd but as 2nd ps. rather than 3rd, as we learn by the verb y─Бthaс╕е late in p─Бda d.

Note c pur┼л╠Бv├бr─Бс╣Гsi, a rhyme form to ur┼л╠Бv├бr─Бс╣Гsi ending 1d.

Griffith

Moving to sacrifice through realms of lustre they light the radiance of the car that bears them.
Traversing many wide unmeasured spaces, over the wastes ye pass, and fields, and waters.

Geldner

Zum Opfer kommend durch die reinen L├╝fte lie├Яen sie den Glanz ihres Wagens leuchten. Viele unerme├Яliche R├дume durchmessend fahret ihr ├╝ber Gew├дsser, W├╝sten, Ebenen.

Grassmann

Zum Opfer eilend mit den lichten Rossen durchdrangen mit des Wagens Glanz die Luft sie; Viel unermessne weite R├дum’ ermessend geht ihr durch Wasser, trockne Lande, Triften.

Elizarenkova

рддрд╛ рд╣ рддреМ рдЦрд▓реБ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рдпрддреН рдЕрд░рдзреНрд░рдореН рдЕрд╕рдореГрджреНрдзрдВ рддреНрдпрддреН рд╡рд░реНрддрд┐рдГ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рддрддреН рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рд╕рдорд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддреБрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдердГ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдЗрддреНрдерд╛ рдЗрддреНрдердВ рдзрд┐рдпрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдиреН рдЗрд╖рд┐рд░реИрдГ рдПрд╖рдгреАрдпреИрдГ рдХрд╛рдореНрдпреИрдГ рдордиреЛрдЬрд╡реЗрднрд┐рдГ рдордиреЛрд╡реЗрдЧреИрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдпреИрд░рд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ рд╢рд╢реНрд╡рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рдКрд╣рдереБрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдердГ ред рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рд╢реБрд╖рдГ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡реНрдпрдерд┐рдГ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХ: рдкрд░рд┐ рд╢рдпрдзреНрдпреИ рдкрд░рд┐рд╢рдпрдирд╛рдп рджреАрд░реНрдШрдирд┐рджреНрд░рд╛рдпреИ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддрд╛рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFierce A┼Ыvins, from thhat humble mansion to which (you have repaired), you have ever borne with your desirable horses, as swift as thought, the pious worshippers in some manner (to heaven); let the injurer of the liberal man (be consigned by you) to (final) repose.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When (you drive) this circuit without slackening, o powerful ones. Over and over you have conveyed insights that are right to the point, with your horses
swift as thought and vigorous, in order to circumscribe the wayward course of the pious mortal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. presents a different type of grammatical disharmony, though it again concerns how to construe the first p─Бda. Once again it begins with du. t─Б╠Б, but in this case that prn. can be the subj. of the 2nd dual pf. ┼лhathuс╕е. (Though by my rules,= I would prefer not to have a 3rd ps. prn serving as subj. to a non-imperatival verb [see my тАЬsa fig├йтАЭ], I do have to reckon with a fairly clear ex. in 6ab.) The problems lie in 1) vart├нс╕е тАШcircuitтАЩ and 2) y├бd. To begin with the 2nd, if y├бd is functioning as a subordinating conjunction and ab is a single clause, ┼лhathuс╕е in b should be accented.

(It is not clear to me what Geldner does with the y├бd; he seems just to ignore it.) Now y├бd is badly positioned for a clausal subordinator, and it is possible that rather than being a subordinating conjunction itтАЩs functioning as a sort of izafe in the phrase ty├бd vart├нr y├бd ├бradhram, connecting the adj. ├бradhram to vart├нс╕е. I would be inclined to that interpr. if it werenтАЩt for the problem of vart├нс╕е itself. This noun is always the complement of the verb тИЪy─Б in the phrase тАЬdrive the/a/your circuit,тАЭ incl. in this same hymn, 10ab тАж vart├нс╕е тАж y─Бtam, and in the next one, with phraseology similar to ours, VI.63.2 p├бri ha ty├бd vart├нr y─Бthaс╕е тАж It would be very difficult to make it the obj. of ┼лhathuс╕е, which already has an obj. of its own in any case. But the preceding p─Бda, 2d, has a form of тИЪy─Б, and I suggest that we simply supply it in 3a as well, which is again pendant on the preceding vs. By this interpr., subordinating y├бd is still badly positioned, but it could have been displaced by the insistently fronted t─Б╠Бin this section of the hymn. I take ├бradhram as a neut. adv., but it could also modify v├бrtiс╕е (тАЬunslackening circuitтАЭ) without benefit of an izafe.

The lexeme p├бri тИЪ┼Ыi means lit. тАШlie aroundтАЩ and is used, e.g., of Vс╣Ыtra surrounding the flood in IV.19.2, etc. Assuming that ┼Ыay├бdhyai, p├бri here belongs to the same lexeme, it must have a developed sense: to surround and thus circumscribe, keep within bounds. Why a тАЬpious mortalтАЭ would be pursuing a course that needs such control is not clear to me. I suppose it could just mean that, since the A┼Ыvins circle around the earth (1cd), that circle marks the boundaries of where humans can wander.

Note the echo effect of v├бrtiс╕е (a) / vy├бthiс╕е (d).

Griffith

Ye to that bounteous path of yours, ye mighty, have ever borne away our thoughts with horses,
Mind-swift and full of vigour, that the trouble of man who offers gifts might cease and slumber.

Geldner

Als solche habt ihr Gewaltige immer wieder diese unerm├╝dliche Umfahrt zu dem darauf rechnenden Sterblichen unternommen, mit den gedankenschnellen eifrigen Rossen, um den Fehltritt des opfernden Sterblichen zu verh├╝ten.

Grassmann

Ihr fuhret stets zur eifervollen Festschar, gewalt’ge mit den Rossen recht zur Andacht, Den geistesschnellen, muntern, um zu ruhen rings bei dem Werk des Mannes, der euch huldigt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHarnessing their horses, bringing excellent food, nourishment, and strength, they approach (to receive) the adoration of their recent worshipper; and may the benevolent ancient invoker of the gods (Agni) sacrifice to the ever youthful (deities).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The two attend upon the thoughts of (me), the newer singer, having harnessed their team,
conveying beauty and fortifying power, refreshment and nourishment. The age-old Hotar without deceit shall offer sacrifice to the two youths.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted ad vs 1., j├бram─Бс╣Зa- here seems to belong to тАШsingтАЩ, not тАШawakenтАЩ, and therefore may limit the form in 1b as well. Based on 1b huve j├бram─Бс╣Зaс╕е тАЬsinging, I call uponтАЭ and 5b ─Б╠Бviv─Бse тАЬI seek to attract,тАЭ I have supplied a 1st ps.

referent for the genitives here. The bahuvr─лhi yuyuj─Бn├б-sapt─л тАШhaving a harnessed team, having a team that has been harnessedтАЩ is unusual in having a middle pf. part. as its first member. (See AiG II.1.43.) The published translation тАЬhaving harnessed their team,тАЭ though it follows both Grassmann and Geldner, is misleading: I do not think it is a bhar├бd-v─Бja-, coday├бn-mati type governing cmpd. I would therefore emend to тАЬhaving a harnessed team,тАЭ with the occasional pass. value of the med. pf. to тИЪyuj; see K├╝mmel (407). However, things may be somewhat more complex. There are four occurrences of this med. part., one nearby in VI.59.5, three in the same metrical position as here (immed. after an opening of 5). All of them are transitive. It is possible that a free phrase like *yuyuj─Бn─Б╠Бs├бpt─л тАЬthe two having yoked their teamsтАЭ became univerbated and reinterpreted, with adjustment of accent and the like. But I do not insist on this.

In d pratn├бс╕е тАШage-oldтАЩ qualifying the priest contrasts with n├бvyas- тАШnewerтАЩ in a, qualifying the singer, as well as y├║v─Бn─Б тАШtwo youthsтАЩ in d referring to the A┼Ыvins. The first pair recurs in the next vs., 5b. See comm. there. The тАЬage-old HotarтАЭ is of course Agni.

Griffith

So ye, when ye have yoked your chariothorses, come to the hymn of the most recent singer.
Our true and ancient Herald Priest shall bring you, the Youthful, bearing splendour, food, and vigour.

Geldner

Sie warten auf das Gebet des j├╝ngsten Fr├╝hbeters, wenn sie ihre Rosse angeschirrt haben. Die Jugendlichen, die Sch├╢nheit, Lebenskraft, Labsal, St├дrkung mitf├╝hren, soll der uralte, nie tr├╝gende Hotri verehren.

Grassmann

Mit Rossen fahrend nahn sie eifrig achtsam dem Andachtslied des neuesten der S├дnger; Herfahrend Schmuck und Labung, Trank und Speise; euch junge ehr der holde, alte Priester.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI worship with a new hymn those two quick-moving good-looking ancient (A┼Ыvins), the achievers of many exploits, who are the givers of great felicity to him who prays to (them), or praises (them); the bestowers of wondrous gifts on him who adores (them).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The two, obliging and skillful, best endowed with many abilitiesтАФthose age-old ones do I seek to attract here with my newer speechтАФ
those two who become most wealful for the reciter and praiser,
providing bright gifts to the singer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The stems n├бvyas- тАШnewerтАЩ and pratn├б- тАШage-oldтАЩ, found at opposite ends of the preceding vs. (a and d), are juxtposed here in the phrase pratn─Б╠Бn├бvyas─Б, in case the duller members of the audience had missed the contrastive terminology in 4. But this phrase is doing two other things as well: du. pratn─Б╠Бrefers to the A┼Ыvins, who were, in 4d, identified as y├║v─Бn─Б тАШyouthsтАЩ; and n├бvyas─Б modifies v├бcas─Б, тАЬwith a newer speech,тАЭ repairing the slightly off phrase in 4a, where it was the singer, not his song, who was newer.

The pf. babh┼лv├бtuс╕е should not have been rendered as a straight pres. in the published translation I would change to тАЬwho have become.тАЭ It also forms a slight figure with ┼Ы├бmbhaviс╣гс╣нh─Б, which precedes it immediately before the p─Бda break.

Griffith

With newest hymn I call those Wonder-Workers, ancient and brilliant, and exceeding mighty,
Bringers of bliss to him who lauds and praises, bestowing varied bounties on the singer.

Geldner

Die sch├╢nen, meisterlichen, vielverm├╢gendsten uralten Asvin bitte ich mit neuester Rede her, die dem Vortragenden und Lobsingenden am meisten gewogen sind und dem Preisenden blinkende Gaben bringen.

Grassmann

Die sch├╢nen, hehren, die an Kr├дften reichsten, die alten ehr’ ich mit dem neusten Liede, Die h├╝lfreich stets dem Dichter, der sie r├╝hmte, dem S├дnger reich an sch├╢nen Gaben waren.

Elizarenkova

рддрд╛ рддрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдВ рддреБрдЧреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрдиреБрдВ рднреБрдЬреНрдпреБрдВ рднреБрдЬреНрдпреБрдирд╛рдордХрдВ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдордзреНрдпреЗ рднрдЧреНрдирдирд╛рд╡рдВ рднреБрдЬрдиреНрддрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреМ рдЕрд░реЗрдгреБрднрд┐рдГ рд░реЗрдгреБрд░рд╣рд┐рддреИрдГ рдЖрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реИрдГ рд░рдЬреЛрднрд┐рдГ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреИрдГ рдпреЛрдЬрдиреЗрднрд┐рдГ рд░рдердпреБрдХреНрддреИрдГ рдкрддрддреНрд░рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкрддрдирд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╡рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╕рдГ рдЬрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдерд╛рддреН рдпреЛрдиреЗрдГ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рддреН рдЕрджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдирд┐: рдКрд╣рдереБрдГ рдирд┐рд░рдЧрдордпрддрдореН ред рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рджрджреНрднреНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рдорд╛рддреБрд░реНрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рджреНрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреАрддрд┐рд╡рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey bore up from te waters, from the ocean, by the winged horses attached to their car, (passing) by roads unsoiled by dust, Bhujyu, the son of Tugra; they (bore them) from out of the lap of the water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Arс╣Зaso nirupasth─Бt, from the womb of the water, jalasya yoneс╕е samudr─Бd abhyo nir agamayatam

Jamison Brereton

You two with your birds conveyed Bhujyu, the son of Tugra, from the waters, from the sea, through the airy realms,
through dustless treks, bending (him) away from the lap of the flood with your winged ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted ad vs. 3, I would prefer not to have the 3rd ps. prn. t─Б╠Бserving as a subject of an indicative 2nd ps. verb (pf. ┼лhathuс╕е), but the repetitive t─Б╠Бpattern may have imposed it here.

The adj. areс╣З├║- тАШdustlessтАЩ (8x) twice qualifies тАШpathsтАЩ (I.35.11, 163.6); the latter of these passages is in the instr. pl. as here. This suggests that y├│janebhiс╕е тАШtreksтАЩ is used here as a near synonym for тАШpathsтАЩ.

Geldner takes bhuj├бnt─Б to тИЪbhuj тАШbenefit, enjoy ├а utilizeтАЩ (benutzen), but better, with Grassmann, Renou, Lubotsky, to тИЪbhuj тАШbendтАЩ. In any case this participle is clearly meant to echo the name Bhujyu.

Griffith

So ye, with birds, out of the sea and waters bore Bhujyu, son of Tugra, through the regions.
Speeding with winged steeds through dustless spaces, out of the bosom of the flood they bore him.

Geldner

Ihr fuhret des Tugra Sohn, den Bhujyu, mit euren Vogelrossen aus dem Wasser, dem Meere durch die L├╝fte, die staublosen Wegestrecken benutzend, mit den gefl├╝gelten aus dem Scho├Яe der Flut.

Grassmann

Ihr fuhrt den Budschju aus des Meeres Fluten, des Tugra Sohn mit V├╢geln durch die L├╝fte, Die unbest├дubten, mit den Fl├╝gelrossen, heraus ihm helfend aus dem Schooss der Meerflut.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRiders in your car, you have penetrated the mountain by your triumphant chariot; showerers (of benefits) you heard the invocation of Vadhrimat─л; you have nourished, bountiful givers, the cow of ┼Ъayu– and in this manner displaying benevolence are you everywhere present.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With your victorious (chariot), you charioteers drove through the rock; you harkened to the call of Vadhr─лmat─л, o bulls.
Showing favor to ┼Ъayu, you made his cow swell. Thus (did you show) your benevolence, you stirring and bustling ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In d I take ├нti as a summarizing device, indicating that the three exploits sketched in abc are examples of the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ sumat├н-. With Geldner I see no choice but to supply a verb like тАШyou showedтАЩ to govern the acc. sumat├нm.

As is clear to all, cy├бv─Бn─Б is at the least a play on the name Cyav─Бna (same accent), another client of the A┼Ыvins.

Griffith

Victors, car-borne, ye rent the rock asunder: Bulls, heard the calling of the eunuch’s consort.
Bounteous, ye filled the cow with milk for Sayu: thus, swift and zealous Ones, ye showed your favour.

Geldner

Mit dem siegreichen Wagen fuhret ihr Wagenlenker durch den Fels; ihr Bullen erh├╢rtet den Ruf der Vadhrimati. Dem Sayu wart ihr gef├дllig und habt seine Kuh milchreich gemacht. Also erwieset ihr euer Wohlwollen, ihr Cyavana┬┤s, ihr Eilige.

Grassmann

Siegreich durchdringt den Fels ihr, Wagenlenker, vernahmt der Vadhrimati Ruf, ihr Helden, Zu Lieb’ dem ├Зaju liesst die Kuh ihr schwellen, so eure Gunst erweisend, o ihr regen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬHeaven and Earth, ─Аdiyas, Vasus, Maruts, rende that dread ange of the gods which (has) of old (been directed) against mortals, destructive and fatal to him who is associated with the r─Бkс╣гasas.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rakс╣гoyuje = r─Бkс╣гasam sv─Бmine prerak─Бya v─Б; rakso.obhir yukt─Бya yajvane, one who sacrifices, assisted or joined by the r─Бkс╣гasas

Jamison Brereton

O world-halves, the anger of gods and among mortals that exists from of old on earth,
direct that evil heat at the yokemate of demons, o ─Аdityas, Vasus, and Rudriyas.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The grammatical identity of bh┼л╠Бm─Б (Pp. bh┼л╠Бma) is disputed. Geldner considers it to belong to a (hapax) adj. stem *bh┼л╠Бman- derived from bh┼лm├бn- тАШabundanceтАЩ, used adverbially (тАЬreichlichтАЭ). This does not seem to have much to recommend it. More appealing is to make it somehow related to a word for тАШearthтАЩ. Renou tries an instr. of bh┼л╠Бman- тАШearthтАЩ, but not with much conviction. Oldenberg rehearses – mostly to firmly reject – other possibilities, incl. the one that I favor: that it is the loc. of bh┼л╠Бmi-. He objects that we should expect (and do indeed get) bh┼л╠Бmy─Бm to this fem. stem, but at this period I donтАЩt think this would be necessary for a fem. short-i-stem. His other object is more cogent, that to a short-i-stem we would expect bh┼л╠Бmau p─Бda-final. I donтАЩt have a clinching arg. against this, but would point out that there is some variation in these patterns. And this p─Бda seems to be playing with the heaven / earth distinction by other means: we first have the two world halves (rodas─л), followed by (pra-)d├нvaс╕е тАж bh┼л╠Бm─Б, which distantly evokes dy─Б╠Бv─Б-bh┼л╠Бm─л. The off-balance pairing is matched by the off-balance pairing of gods and mortals discussed immediately below.

The conjoined NP dev─Б╠Бn─Бm ut├б martyatr─Б╠БтАЬof gods and among mortalsтАЭ shows the familiar god / mortal opposition, but what Klein (DGRV I.311-12) calls тАЬa peculiar absence of morphological parallelism.тАЭ It is tempting to make it mean тАЬthe anger of the gods towards mortals,тАЭ but I think ut├б is there precisely to block that reading, pace Scarlatta (429) тАЬDen Groll der G├╢tter тАж der auch auf die Sterblichen gerichtet тАжist.тАЭ

Griffith

English translation:

тАЬMitra and Varuс╣Зa recognize him who of all the world worships the royal (A┼Ыvins) in due season; he hurls his weapon against the strong r─Бkс╣гasa, against the malignant menaces of man.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Drogh─Бya cid vacase ─Бnav─Бya = abhidroh─Бtmak─Бya manuс╣гyasambhandine vacan─Бya eva

Jamison Brereton

Which (one of) the two kings, Mitra or Varuс╣Зa, will keep watch over the airy realm, regulating it according to the proper sequenceтАФ
hurl your missile at the deep-embedded demonic power and also at the deceitful speech of the Anu people.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the syntax of this vs. is unregulated. However, the sense is quite clear. The first hemistich consists of a rel. clause, whose rel. prn.

and finite verb are both in the 3rd sg.: y├бс╕е тАж c├нketat тАЬwho will keep watchтАЭ; it also contains another verbal form, vid├бdhat, which I take, with Geldner and Oldenberg, as a pres.

part. nom. sg. m. to the redupl. pres. of тИЪdh─Б, but which could be, as Oldenberg points out, a short-vowel subjunctive (so, тАЬтАж will regulate тАж and will keep watchтАЭ). (Nothing rides on the choice.) But this happy singular environment is interrupted by a dual nom./acc. (which must be nom. in this case) r─Б╠Бj─Бnau тАЬtwo kings,тАЭ which is further specified by the two nom. singulars mitr├│ v├бruс╣Зaс╕е. The sense is clearly тАЬwhich one (of) the two kings, M (or) V тАж,тАЭ but this is not what it says: тАЬwhich one, the two kings, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, will keep watch,тАЭ leaving the audience to choose what subject, in what number, it prefers.

I take r├бjasaс╕е as the gen. obj. of c├нketat (so also Oldenberg), in the usual syntactic pattern of verbs of perception, which can take acc. or gen. complements. By contrast, Geldner has it dependent on r─Б╠Бj─Бn─Бu, but, as Renou points out, the two are rather distant, and further I know of no other passages in which r├бjas- is construed with r─Б╠Бjan-, although that expression would be appealingly alliterative – though it is true that M+V are called dhart─Б╠Бr─Б r├бjasaс╕е тАЬupholders of the spaceтАЭ in V.69.4.

The second hemistich has no direct syntactic connection to the first, though again it is quite clear what is meant. It contains a 2nd sg. impv. asya тАШhurlтАЩ, which must be addressed to the referent of the rel. prn. in ab – that is, either Mitra or Varuс╣Зa. Although it is common to change person reference even within RVic vss., it is somewhat unusual to do so in this kind of syntagm. In d Renou calls the phrase dr├│gh─Бya cid v├бcase a bahuvr─лhi тАЬd├йfait,тАЭ for *droghavacas- [he gives no accent], like drogha-v─Б╠Бc-. Judging from his tr. тАЬauf den gar verlogenen Anuiden,тАЭ Geldner seems to agree. But this seems unnec.; the dative targets of the missile in c and d are both s-stem abstracts, r├бkс╣гas- тАШdemonic powerтАЩ and v├бcas- тАШspeechтАЩ respectively. I see no reason to try to manipulate the target in d to be personal. Scarlatta (469) interpr. as I do.

Griffith

May he who knows, as Varuna and Mitra, air’s realm, appointing both the Kings in season,
Against the secret fiend cast forth his weapon, against the lying words that strangers utter.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реИрдГ рдЕрдирд┐рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреИрдГ рдЪрдХреНрд░реИрдГ рдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрди рджреНрдпреБрдорддрд╛ рджреАрдкреНрддрд┐рдорддрд╛ рдиреГрд╡рддрд╛ рдиреЗрддреНрд░рд╛ рд╕рд╛рд░рдерд┐рдирд╛ рдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрди ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрди ред ‘рдкрддрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдГ рдирд░рдГ’ (рдирд┐. рез. резрек. реиреи ) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреН ред рд░рдереЗрди рд╡рд░реНрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рддрдирдпрд╛рдп рддрдирдпрдВ рджрд╛рддреБрдореН рдЖ рдпрд╛рддрдореН ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╕рдиреБрддреНрдпреЗрди рддрд┐рд░реЛрд╣рд┐рддреЗрди рддреНрдпрдЬрд╕рд╛ рдХреНрд░реЛрдзреЗрди ред ‘рд╣реГрдгрд┐рдГ рддреНрдпрдЬрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреНрд░реЛрдзрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрд╛рдард╛рддреНред рдорд░реНрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рдиреБрд╖реНрдпрддрд╛рдВ рдмрд╛рдзрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН ред ‘рд╡рдиреБрд╖реНрдпрддрд┐рд░реНрд╣рдиреНрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХреЗрдиреЛрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖рд╛ рд╢рд┐рд░рд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╡рд╡реГрдХреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрдХреНрддрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome with your shining and well-guided chariot, (fitted) with excellen wheels, to our dwelling, (to bestow upon us) male offspring; cut off with secret indignation the heads of those obstructing (the adoration) of the mortal (who worships you).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Well-guided chariot: nс╣Ыvata rathena, having a leader, a driver; or nr. may mean a horse; with excellen wheels: antarai┼Ыcakraiс╕е: anikс╣Ыс╣гс╣нaiс╕е, with not inferior wheels; with secret indignation: sanutyena tyajas─Б = tirohitena krodhena

Jamison Brereton

With your wheels drawing nearer, with your heaven-bright chariot with its superior men, do you two drive your circuit for our lineage (to prosper),
because of the distant dereliction of a(nother) mortal. Chop off the heads of the rapacious ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I supply тАШto prosperтАЩ with t├бnay─Бya on the basis of nearby VI.49.5 (=I.183.3) тАж iс╣гay├бdhyai, vart├нr y─Бth├бs t├бnay─Бya tm├бne ca, with very similar phraseology.

I take p─Бda c with ab, rather than with d, as is the norm (Geldner, K├╝mmel [509]), in order to capture the opposition between ├бntara- тАШnearerтАЩ and s├бnutya- тАШdistantтАЩ. Cf., e.g., VI.5.4, which has both ├бntara- and s├бnutya- as well as vanuс╣гy├б-. By my interpr. the A┼Ыvins are urged to come near to us, тАЬbecause of the distant dereliction of a(nother) mortalтАЭ – that is, because some other mortal, far away, hasn’t done his ritual duty, they should come to us, who will. I suppose I could construct a way to take c with d: some mortalтАЩs dereliction of duty would cause the A┼Ыvins to chop off some heads.

But I find it easier to account for c as presented. The last, independent p─Бda just takes part in the general bloodthirstiness of the last few vss.

Against Geldner, who takes it to тИЪvс╣Ыj, I assign vavс╣Ыktam to тИЪvra┼Ыc тАШhewтАЩ, along with Whit (Rts), Grassmann, Renou, and K├╝mmel, inter alia. Cf. the clinching parallel in X.87.16 t├йс╣г─Бс╣Г ┼Ы─лrс╣г─Б╠Бс╣Зi тАж ├бpi vс╣Ы┼Ыca.

Griffith

Come to our home with friendly wheels, for offipring; come on your radiant chariot rich in heroes.
Strike off, ye Twain, the heads of our assailants who with man’s treacherous attack approach us.

Geldner

Unternehmet eure Umfahrt auf dem gl├дnzenden, m├дnnertragenden Wagen mit den inneren R├дdern f├╝r unser Geschlecht. Beladet mit der heimlichen Schuld des Sterblichen die H├дupter der Neider!

Grassmann

Mit nah’nden R├дdern und mit lichtem Wagen, der Helden f├дhrt, kommt her zu unsrer St├дtte, Mit weithin reichendem Geschoss des Menschen schiesst ab die K├╢pfe derer, die uns feind sind.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome down, whether with the most excellent, or middling, or inferior Niyut steeds; set upon the doors of the fast-shut stall of the cattle; eb bountiful to him who praises you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Drive here with your highest and midmost teams, this way with your lowest. Open the doors of the cattle pen, even though they are shut fast, you who provide bright gifts for the singer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the last phrase of the hymn, gс╣Ыс╣Зat├й citrar─Бt─л тАЬyou two providing bright gifts for the singerтАЭ exactly repeats the end of vs. 5, which marked a transition in the earlier part of the hymn.

Griffith

Come hitherward to us with teams of horses, the highest and the midmost and the lowest.
Bountiful Lords, throw open to the singer doors e’en of the firm-closed stall of cattle.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рд░рд╛рддреА) рдЕрджреНрднреБрдд рджрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕рднрд╛рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреАрд╢реЛ ! рддреБрдо (рдЕрд╡рдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдирд┐рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯ (рдордзреНрдпрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдордзреНрдпрдо (рдЙрдд) рдФрд░ (рдкрд░рдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдЙрддреНрддрдо (рдирд┐рдпреБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдХреА рдЧрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдЖ, рдпрд╛рддрдореН) рдЖрдУ рддрдерд╛ (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдХреН) рдкреАрдЫреЗ (рджреГрд│реНрд╣рд╕реНрдп) рдЕрддрд┐ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдХреЗ (рдЪрд┐рддреН) рднреА (рдЧреЛрдорддрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд рдЧреМрдпреЗрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЗрдВ рдЬрд┐рд╕рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рди рдЙрд╕ (рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╕реНрдп) рдореЗрдШ рдХреЗ (рджреБрд░рдГ) рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╡рд┐, рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдореН) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдУ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕рдм рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓ рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдХреА рдЧрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдЬрд╛рддреЗ-рдЖрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдФрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкреАрдЬрди рд╡рд┐рдорд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдореЗрдШрдордгреНрдбрд▓ рдкрд░ рдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рддреБрдо рднреА рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рди рдХрд░реЛ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдмрд╛рд╕рдард╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рджреВрд╕рд░рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рд░рд╛рддреА рд╕рднрд╛рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢реМ ! рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдорд╡рдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдордзреНрдпрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реБрдд рдкрд░рдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдирд┐рдпреБрджреНрднрд┐рд░рд╛ рдпрд╛рддрдорд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЧреН рджреГрд│реНрд╣рд╕реНрдп рдЪрд┐рджреН рдЧреЛрдорддреЛ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрд╕реНрдп рджреБрд░реЛ рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ рд╡рд┐ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдореН реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддреЗ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдкрд░рдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рдЙрдд) (рдордзреНрдпрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдордзреНрдпреЗ рднрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рдирд┐рдпреБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрд░реНрдЧрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ (рдпрд╛рддрдореН) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрдореН (рдЕрд╡рдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рдирд┐рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдХреН) рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреН (рджреГрд│реНрд╣рд╕реНрдп) (рдЪрд┐рддреН) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рдЧреЛрдорддрдГ) рдмрд╣реНрд╡реНрдпреЛ рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдп (рд╡рд┐) (рд╡реНрд░рдЬрд╕реНрдп) рдореЗрдШрд╕реНрдп (рджреБрд░рдГ) рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рдгрд┐ (рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдореН) рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдпрддрдореН (рдЧреГрдгрддреЗ) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХрд╛рдп (рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рд░рд╛рддреА) рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╜рджреНрднреБрддрд╛ рд░рд╛рддрд┐рд░реНрджрд╛рдирдВ рдпрдпреЛрд╕реНрддреМ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдЧрддрд┐рднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛ рдЪ рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рдорд╛рдиреЗрди рдореЗрдШрдордгреНрдбрд▓реЛрдкрд░рд┐ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдереИрд╡ рдпреВрдпрдордкреНрдпрдиреБрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╣реЛ ! рдЬрд╕реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓ рд╡рд╛рдпреВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЧрддреАрдмрд░реЛрдмрд░ рдлрд┐рд░рдд рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд рд╡ рдЬрд╕реЗ рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкреАрдЬрди (рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдЧреАрд░) рд╡рд┐рдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреЗ рдореЗрдШрдордВрдбрд│рд╛рддреВрди рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдд рддрд╕реЗ рддреБрдореНрд╣реАрд╣реА рд╡рд╛рдЧрд╛. рее резрез рее
